The section of sam'iyyat (audible matters). Because it is bad manners with God. Riya' (show-off) accompanies it and corrupts it (1). And indeed 'ujb (self-admiration) is prohibited; (1) Most High, for it is not befitting for the servant to magnify what he draws near with to his Master, rather he should consider it small relative to the greatness of his Master, especially His greatness. He said, Most High: {And they did not esteem God with the estimation due to Him} [al-An'am: 91], meaning: they did not magnify Him with true magnification. And similar to 'ujb (2) are: tyranny (dhulm), oppression (baghy) (3), highway robbery (hirabah), cheating (ghishsh), deception (khadi'ah) (4), lying without a religious benefit (5), abandoning prayer, withholding zakah, and being undutiful to parents. (1) His saying: (corrupts it) this indicates that riya' corrupts the action, such that it does not suffice to discharge the duty, rather its repetition is required. But some investigators have stated that it merely nullifies the reward, while the action itself is valid. al-Shanwani. (2) His saying: (And similar to 'ujb) i.e., in being a blameworthy trait. This explains what the kaf (the letter 'like') includes. And the author specifically mentioned what he did, even though it is not part of the art... due to his concern for the faults of the soul, for their persistence along with the outward reformation is like wearing beautiful clothes over a body soiled with filth. al-Amir. (3) His saying: (al-baghy) lexically means exceeding the limit, and legally it is disobeying the imam. al-Shanwani. (4) His saying: (al-hirabah) i.e., highway robbery. His saying: (al-ghishsh) is deceiving people, such as mixing the bad with the good. It is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, passed by a man selling food, and he admired it, so he inserted his hand and found wetness. He said: 'What is this, O seller of food?' He said: 'Rain fell on it.' He said: 'Did you not put it on top so that people could see it?' Then he said: 'Whoever cheats is not of me,' i.e., not upon my complete path. His saying: (al-khadi'ah) is making someone imagine contrary to what you conceal of harm, such as making the product seem good while hiding its defect. al-Shanwani. (5) His saying: (without a religious benefit) and as for if it is for a religious benefit, it is permissible, such as lying to the disbelievers about war, if one intends thereby to terrify them, for it is recommended, and such as lying to reconcile between Muslims. It was said: and lying to one's wife to please her heart. al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the discussion on sam'iyyat (matters of revelation). It defines 'ujb (self-admiration) and states its ruling, then lists other sins similar in being blameworthy. The author begins by stating that riya' (show-off) corrupts an action. Then he explains why 'ujb is prohibited: a servant should not magnify his own good deeds but rather consider them insignificant before God's greatness. He cites the verse 'They did not esteem God with the estimation due to Him.' After this, he lists sins that resemble 'ujb: tyranny, oppression, highway robbery, cheating, deception, lying without religious benefit, abandoning prayer, withholding zakah, and being undutiful to parents. The footnotes clarify details: (1) discusses whether riya' corrupts the action itself or just the reward, (2) explains that the author's mention of these sins is due to their being inner faults, (3-4) give definitions of baghy, hirabah, ghishsh, and khadi'ah, and (5) notes exceptions for permissible lying. This lesson thus covers a set of major sins connected to the heart and outward conduct.

الحرابة (al-hirabah)
الغش (al-ghishsh)
الخديعة (al-khadi'ah)
الكذب (al-kadhib)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Self-admiration and show-off are minor sins that don't affect salvation.
Correction: The passage classifies 'ujb as bad manners with God, and riya' corrupts actions, indicating they are serious spiritual diseases that must be avoided.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Self-admiration (ujb) is a serious sin because it involves forgetting God's greatness, and it is similar to many other major sins that stem from the soul's corruption.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The author lists sins like oppression, lying without benefit, and abandoning prayer as resembling 'ujb. Which of these might you be guilty of, even in a subtle way, while considering it minor? Will you repent and make a firm resolve to avoid it starting now?
?
When you reflect on your life, do you find yourself more focused on your own deeds or on God's greatness? The lesson says 'ujb comes from not esteeming God properly. What specific change in your daily routine can you make to constantly magnify God in your heart?

Definition and Ruling of Kibr (Pride)
The author defines kibr and states its prohibition, citing the hadith and distinguishing two targets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic definition of kibr (pride) and its two-fold ruling: forbidden towards the righteous and required towards the enemies of Allah.

Core Idea
Pride is rejecting truth and despising people, not beauty.

This lesson presents the clear prophetic definition of kibr (pride) and its ruling. The author cites the famous hadith where the Prophet ﷺ explains that kibr is not about loving beauty, but about rejecting the truth and looking down on others. He then distinguishes between kibr towards the righteous (forbidden) and towards oppressors (required).

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith definition carefully
The Prophet ﷺ defines kibr as 'batar al-haqq' (rejecting the truth) and 'ghamz an-nas' (despising people). Notice that this excludes outward beautification.
2
Understand the ruling on kibr
Kibr towards the righteous and Muslim leaders is a major sin. But kibr towards enemies of Allah and oppressors is required—this means we should despise their evil states.
This shows that the ruling depends on whom it is directed at.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Do you reject advice out of pride? Do you belittle others? This definition goes to the heart of character.
Kibr is a spiritual disease.

Definition of Kibr (pride) and exposition of its prohibition. (Al-kibr) is 'batar al-haqq' (rejecting the truth) and 'ghamz an-nas' (despising people), according to the hadith: 'None will enter Paradise who has an atom's weight of pride in his heart.' They said: O Messenger of God, one of us loves to have his garment and sandal beautiful. He said: 'Indeed God is Beautiful and loves beauty (2), but indeed kibr is refusing the truth and despising people' – with the unpointed sad and ta'. And 'batar al-haqq' is rejecting it from its speaker, and 'ghamz an-nas' is looking down on them (4). And kibr towards the righteous and the imams of the Muslims is forbidden, counted among the major sins (kaba'ir), and it is among the greatest of sins of the heart. And towards the enemies of God (5) and the oppressors, it is required. (1) His saying: (it is batar al-haqq) i.e., not accepting it; i.e., it is from its effects and signs, otherwise kibr is an attribute in the soul from which that arises. al-Shanwani. And batar: with the vowel fat-ha on the ba' and the daal. (2) His saying: (Beautiful) i.e., described with the attributes of beauty, which are the positive attributes. His saying: (loves beauty) i.e., He rewards a person for manifesting blessings. So one who beautifies himself with clothes, mounts, houses, servants, and palaces – it is not necessarily kibr; rather it is obligatory for rulers and others if the execution of duty depends on it, for a shabby appearance for rulers and others does not allow for the public interest nowadays, because souls in later ages have been habituated to respect based on appearance, contrary to the early righteous who respected based on religion and piety. And it is recommended in prayers, congregations, and wars to terrify the enemy, and for a woman for her husband, and for scholars to venerate knowledge in people's hearts. And it is forbidden if it is a means to something forbidden, like one who adorns himself for foreign women leading to immorality with them. And it is disliked if it is for outdoing one's peers. And it is permissible if free of these reasons and not intending to show off blessings. al-Shanwani. (3) His saying: (and ghamz an-nas) with the sad as narrated by al-Tirmidhi, and ghamt an-nas with the ta' as narrated by Muslim. al-Shanwani. (4) His saying: (looking down on them) i.e., belittling them and being careless with their rights. al-Shanwani. (5) His saying: (and towards the enemies of God) i.e., the disbelievers. The intended meaning of kibr towards them is despising them for what they are upon of disbelief and disobedience, so one hates their state in word and deed, not despising their essence. al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage defines kibr (pride) and explains its ruling. The author begins by stating the definition: kibr is 'batar al-haqq' (rejecting the truth) and 'ghamz an-nas' (despising people). He cites the well-known hadith that no one with even an atom's weight of pride will enter Paradise, and the Prophet's clarification that beautifying oneself is not pride, but rather pride is rejecting truth and despising people. The author then gives the exact meanings: 'batar al-haqq' means refusing to accept the truth from the one who says it, and 'ghamz an-nas' means looking down on people. He then distinguishes two cases: kibr towards the righteous and Muslim leaders is forbidden and is a major sin of the heart; but kibr towards the enemies of God and oppressors is required (i.e., it is desirable to despise them for their evil). The footnotes expand on these points: (1) explains that 'batar al-haqq' is a sign of kibr, not its essence; (2) gives a detailed ruling on beautification, showing when it is obligatory, recommended, forbidden, disliked, or permissible; (3) notes variant readings of the hadith; (4) defines 'ghamz' as belittling; and (5) clarifies that despising disbelievers is about their states, not their persons.

Key Terms
الكبر (al-kibr)
بطر الحق (batar al-haqq)
غمص الناس/غمط الناس (ghamz/ghamt an-nās)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any form of beautification or self-respect is kibr (pride).
Correction: The Prophet ﷺ explicitly distinguishes between loving beauty (which is permissible) and pride, which is rejecting truth and despising people.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, what is the meaning of kibr (pride)?
A) Wearing beautiful clothes
B) Being arrogant and boastful
C) Rejecting the truth and despising people
D) Feeling superior to others

Key Takeaway
Kibr is defined by the Prophet as rejecting the truth and despising people; it is a major sin when directed at the righteous, but required when directed at the enemies of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are corrected by someone you consider less knowledgeable or lower in status, do you feel a resistance in your heart? That is the 'batar al-haqq'. What truth have you rejected recently because of who said it? Will you go back and accept it now?
?
The Prophet ﷺ said that an atom's weight of kibr prevents entry into Paradise. Pause and scan your heart: toward whom do you feel a sense of superiority? Can you pinpoint whether that feeling is due to their sin (which you may rightly dislike) or due to their person (which is kibr)? How will you untangle that today?
?
The lesson teaches that kibr towards enemies of Allah is required in the sense of hating their kufr, not their essence. Are you able to separate your hatred of someone's evil deeds from contempt for them as a person? When you look at a sinner, does your heart lean toward arrogance or mercy? What would change if you truly internalized this distinction?

Affirmation of Afterlife Beliefs and Intercession
Author affirms bodily resurrection, punishment, intercession, and eternal punishment only for disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni stance on bodily resurrection, the realities of the grave and afterlife events, the distinction between disbelievers and sinful believers regarding eternal punishment, and the affirmation of pardon and intercession.

Core Idea
The afterlife is real; only disbelievers suffer eternally; intercession is by Allah's grace.

This passage from Ibn Jawhari's poem concisely states key Sunni eschatological beliefs. It affirms bodily resurrection and all that revelation has conveyed about the grave, judgment, and the path. Importantly, it distinguishes between the eternal fate of disbelievers and sinful believers, and it affirms the truth of pardon and intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the compact style and the three distinct affirmations.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the three affirmations
The passage makes three points: 1) affirmation of bodily resurrection and all reported events, 2) eternal punishment for disbelievers only, 3) truth of pardon and intercession.
3
Consider the exclusion of sinful believers
Why does the author specifically say 'but not the sinful believers'? This refutes groups who claim Muslims who sin are eternally punished.
This is a key Sunni position.
4
Reflect on intercession
Intercession is affirmed as true, but it is by Allah's grace and pardon. Understand that it benefits only believers, not disbelievers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنَّ المعاد الجسماني وسائرَ ما ورد به السَّمعُ مِن عذاب القبر والحِساب والميزان والصِّراط وغير ذلك حق . وأن الكفار مخلدون في النَّار دونَ الفُسَّاق مِن المؤمنين، وأن العفو والشَّفاعة حقٌّ بفضل الله تعالى وعفوه .
And that the bodily resurrection and all that is reported by revelation of the punishment of the grave, the reckoning, the scale, the path, and others are true. And that the disbelievers are eternally in the Fire, but not the sinful believers; and that pardon and intercession are true by the grace and pardon of Allah.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is a statement of Sunni eschatology. It affirms the bodily resurrection (ma'ad jismani) and other events reported in revelation: punishment of the grave (adhab al-qabr), reckoning (hisab), scale (mizan), path (sirat), etc. It then distinguishes between disbelievers (kuffar) and sinful believers (fussaq): disbelievers are eternally in Hell, while sinful believers are not — a refutation of Kharijite and Mu'tazilite views that sinful believers may be eternally punished. Finally, it affirms that pardon (afw) and intercession (shafa'a) are true, by the grace of Allah, rejecting those who deny intercession.

Key Terms
معاد جسماني
عذاب القبر
حساب
ميزان
صراط
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is unconditional and applies to all sinners, including disbelievers.
Correction: The passage explicitly states disbelievers are eternally punished, so intercession does not apply to them. It is by Allah's grace for believers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who will be eternally in Hellfire?
A) All sinners
B) Disbelievers only
C) Both disbelievers and sinful believers
D) Only those who deny intercession

Key Takeaway
Bodily resurrection and all revealed afterlife events are true; only disbelievers are eternally in Hell; intercession and pardon are real by Allah's grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage states that only disbelievers are eternally in Hell. Do you truly believe that your sins will not condemn you eternally as a believer, or do you secretly doubt Allah's mercy? How does this certainty affect the way you repent and strive to avoid sin today?
?
Intercession is true but only by Allah's grace and pardon—not earned by any human. Are you relying on someone's intercession (like a saint or scholar) as a safety net instead of directly seeking Allah's forgiveness? Will you sincerely repent today without depending on any intermediary?
?
The afterlife events (grave punishment, reckoning, scale, path) are not mere symbols; they are real and imminent. Which of these events do you find yourself ignoring or downplaying? What concrete step will you take this week to prepare for that event?

Affirming the Major Portents of the Hour
Author affirms five specific major portents of the Hour as true.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five major eschatological signs (ashrat al-sa'a) that Sunni Muslims affirm as true, as listed by the author.

Core Idea
The major portents of the Hour are true and must be believed.

In this passage, the author explicitly affirms the truth of several major signs that will precede the Day of Judgment. These include the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the sun rising from the west, and the beast of the earth. Let's read the text and see how these are presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then read the English translation. Notice the concise style — each sign is simply listed without elaboration.
The word 'حق' (true) at the beginning and end emphasizes their certainty.
2
Identify each sign mentioned
List the five signs as they appear: the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the sun rising from the west, and the beast of the earth.
3
Understand the theological import
Recognize that affirming these signs as true is a requirement of Sunni creed. The passage does not explain them further; belief itself is sufficient.
These are major signs; the text does not mention minor signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنَّ أشراط الساعة حقٌّ؛ مِن خُروج الدَّجال ويأجوج ومأجوج ونزول عيسى، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخروج دابَّة الأرض حق. وأوَّلُ الأنبياء آدم، وآخرهم محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وأوَّلُ الخلفاء أبو بكر،
And that the portents of the Hour are true: the emergence of the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the rising of the sun from its west, and the emergence of the beast of the earth. And the first of the prophets is Adam, and the last is Muhammad (peace be upon him), and the first of the caliphs is Abu Bakr.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage lists the eschatological signs (ashrat al-sa'a) that Sunni Muslims affirm as true. It mentions specific major signs: the emergence of the Dajjal (Antichrist), Gog and Magog (Ya'juj wa Ma'juj), the descent of Jesus (nuzul 'Isa) from heaven, the sun rising from the west, and the emergence of the beast (dabbat al-ard). Then it states the identities of the first and last prophets (Adam and Muhammad) and the first caliph (Abu Bakr). This affirms the Sunni position on the order of prophetic and caliphal succession.

Key Terms

يأجوج ومأجوج

دابة الأرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the eschatological signs are symbolic or metaphorical.
Correction: The text explicitly states they are 'حق' (true), affirming their literal occurrence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a portent of the Hour in the passage?
A) Dajjal
B) Gog and Magog
C) Appearance of the Mahdi
D) Descent of Jesus

Key Takeaway
The passage affirms the literal truth of five major eschatological signs: Dajjal, Gog and Magog, descent of Jesus, sun rising from west, and beast of the earth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the sun will one day rise from the west, or do you subconsciously treat it as a distant myth? If you knew it would happen tomorrow, what would you change about your life today?
?
The Dajjal will deceive nearly everyone. What weakness in your own faith might make you vulnerable to his fitnah? Name one concrete step you will take this week to fortify your heart against his deception.
?
The descent of Jesus is a sign we anticipate. Are you living as if that day could come at any moment? If not, what is holding you back from the urgency the early Muslims felt?

Affirming the First and Last Prophet and the First Caliph
Author states the first and last prophets and the first caliph.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the first prophet (Adam), the last prophet (Muhammad), and the first caliph (Abu Bakr).

Core Idea
The first prophet is Adam, the last is Muhammad, and the first caliph is Abu Bakr.

Having discussed eschatological signs, the author now turns to the ranks of prophets and caliphs. This brief statement establishes the Sunni consensus on the beginning and end of prophethood and the beginning of the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the parallel structure: 'first...Adam', 'last...Muhammad', 'first...Abu Bakr'.
2
Identify the three claims
The passage makes three distinct claims: Adam is the first prophet, Muhammad is the last prophet, and Abu Bakr is the first caliph. Understand each one.
This opposes Shia claims that Ali was the first caliph or that prophethood continues.
3
Reflect on doctrinal significance
Consider why these statements are included in a creed. They establish clear boundaries: prophethood began with Adam and ended with Muhammad, and the caliphate began with Abu Bakr.

Source Text

Evil Acts and Divine Will
Affirmation that evil acts are not by God's pleasure, command, or love.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that evil actions are not attributed to God's pleasure, command, or love.

Core Idea
Evil is not from God's will in the sense of approval.

Sanusi begins with a crucial clarification: while God creates all actions, evil acts are not by His pleasure or command. This upholds divine transcendence and justice. Let's examine this foundational creedal point.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic sentence
Read the Arabic phrase carefully. Note the negation 'ليسَت' before 'بِرِضَاهُ وَأَمْرِهِ وَمَحَبِّتِهِ'.
2
Understand the triple negation
The passage denies three attributes: pleasure, command, and love. Ask why each is denied for evil acts.
This prevents attributing evil to God's will in a moral sense.
3
Connect to divine transcendence
Reflect on how this protects God from being associated with evil. This is a key Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنَّ القبائح منها ليست برضَاهُ وأمرِهِ ومحبّتِهِ .
وأنَّ المعاد الجسماني وسائرَ ما ورد به السَّمعُ مِن عذاب القبر والحِساب والميزان والصِّراط وغير ذلك حق .
وأن الكفار مخلدون في النَّار دونَ الفُسَّاق مِن المؤمنين، وأن العفو والشَّفاعة حقٌّ بفضل الله تعالى وعفوه .
وأنَّ أشراط الساعة حقٌّ ؛ مِن خُروج الدَّجال ويأجوج ومأجوج ونزول عيسى ، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخروج دابَّة الأرض حق .
وأوَّلُ الأنبياء آدم ، وآخرهم محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وأوَّلُ الخلفاء أبو بكر، ثمَّ عمر ، ثمَّ عثمان ، ثمَّ عليّ رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، والأفضلية بهذا الترتيب كما عرفت .
But evil acts are not by His pleasure, command, and love. And that bodily resurrection and all that is conveyed by revelation from the punishment of the grave, the accounting, the scale, the path, and other than that is true. And that the disbelievers are eternally [abiding] in the Fire, not the sinners among the believers, and that pardon and intercession are true by the grace of God Most High and His forgiveness. And that the signs of the Hour are true: from the emergence of the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the rising of the sun from its west, and the emergence of the beast of the earth, [all] true. And the first of the prophets is Adam, and the last of them is Muhammad, peace be upon him, and the first of the caliphs is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, may God be pleased with them all, and excellence is in this order as you have known.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is a creedal enumeration of Sunni beliefs. It begins by clarifying that evil actions are not attributed to God's pleasure, command, or love, upholding divine transcendence. Then it affirms the truth of bodily resurrection and all eschatological realities reported by revelation: the punishment of the grave, the accounting, the scale, and the path. It then states that disbelievers will abide eternally in Hell, whereas sinful believers will not, and that intercession and pardon are true by God's grace. Next, it lists the major signs of the Hour: the emergence of the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the rising of the sun from the west, and the beast of the earth—all true. Finally, it identifies Adam as the first prophet and Muhammad as the last, and it affirms the order and superiority of the four caliphs: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali, with excellence according to that sequence as is known.

Key Terms
القبائح
رضا
أمر
محبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because God creates evil, He approves of it.
Correction: The text explicitly denies that evil acts are by His pleasure, command, or love.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT denied of God regarding evil acts?
A) His pleasure
B) His command
C) His knowledge
D) His love

Key Takeaway
Evil acts are not by God's pleasure, command, or love, preserving His transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever think 'It must be God's will' to feel less guilty? How does this passage challenge that excuse and demand repentance instead?
?
Think of one evil act you have done. Do you truly believe that God does not love that act? How does that reality affect your confidence in seeking His forgiveness?
?
If God never commands evil, then why do you sometimes feel inclined to do wrong? What does this lesson teach you about examining your own desires rather than blaming God?

Bodily Resurrection and Eschatological Realities
Affirmation of bodily resurrection and other revelation-based eschatological truths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will affirm the truth of bodily resurrection and all eschatological realities conveyed by revelation.

Core Idea
Bodily resurrection and the grave's punishment are true.

After clarifying divine attributes, Sanusi turns to eschatology. He affirms that bodily resurrection and all that revelation has reported about the afterlife—from the punishment of the grave to the scale and path—are true. This lesson covers the core Sunni beliefs about the hereafter.

Guided Path
1
List the eschatological items
Identify each item mentioned: bodily resurrection, punishment of the grave, accounting, scale, path. Write them down.
These are the sam'iyyāt (matters known only through revelation).
2
Understand 'sā'ir' (all that)
The phrase 'wa sā'ira mā warada bihi as-sam‘u' indicates that the list is not exhaustive. Every revealed eschatological detail is true.
3
Reflect on the importance
Why is affirming these matters essential? They are part of the unseen world (ghayb) that faith requires accepting.

Eternal Fate: Disbelievers and Sinful Believers
Affirmation of eternal Hell for disbelievers but not sinful believers, and truth of pardon and intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that disbelievers are eternally in Hell, while sinful believers are not eternal, and that pardon and intercession are true.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are eternal in Hell, sinful believers are not.

Sanusi now distinguishes the fates of disbelievers and sinful believers. He affirms that pardon and intercession are real, by God's grace. This clarifies a central Sunni position on the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish two groups
Note the contrast: 'al-kuffār' (disbelievers) are eternally in Fire, while 'al-fussāq' (sinful believers) are not.
2
Understand the exception
The phrase 'dūna al-fussāq min al-mu’minīn' shows sinful believers are not treated like disbelievers.
This is a key difference from the Kharijite view.
3
Affirm pardon and intercession
Pardon (al-‘afw) and intercession (ash-shafā‘ah) are true by God's grace. Reflect on the role of intercession.

Major Signs of the Hour
Listing major signs of the Hour and affirming their truth.

Learning Objective

The signs of the Hour are true: Dajjal, Gog and Magog, Jesus' descent, etc.

Prophets and the Rightly Guided Caliphs
Identification of first and last prophets and order of caliphs with their superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the first and last prophets and the order and superiority of the four caliphs.

Core Idea
Adam is first prophet, Muhammad last; caliphs' order: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali.

Sanusi concludes the passage by identifying the first and last prophets and affirming the order of the four caliphs. This establishes the Sunni position on prophetic lineage and caliphal precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify first and last prophets
Adam is the first prophet, Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the last. Note that this is a fundamental creedal point.
2
Learn the order of caliphs
Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. This order reflects their excellence.
3
Understand 'al-afḍaliyyah'
The superiority (afḍaliyyah) follows the same order. This counters rival claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنَّ القبائح منها ليست برضَاهُ وأمرِهِ ومحبّتِهِ .
وأنَّ المعاد الجسماني وسائرَ ما ورد به السَّمعُ مِن عذاب القبر والحِساب والميزان والصِّراط وغير ذلك حق .
وأن الكفار مخلدون في النَّار دونَ الفُسَّاق مِن المؤمنين، وأن العفو والشَّفاعة حقٌّ بفضل الله تعالى وعفوه .
وأنَّ أشراط الساعة حقٌّ ؛ مِن خُروج الدَّجال ويأجوج ومأجوج ونزول عيسى ، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخروج دابَّة الأرض حق .
وأوَّلُ الأنبياء آدم ، وآخرهم محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وأوَّلُ الخلفاء أبو بكر، ثمَّ عمر ، ثمَّ عثمان ، ثمَّ عليّ رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، والأفضلية بهذا الترتيب كما عرفت .
But evil acts are not by His pleasure, command, and love. And that bodily resurrection and all that is conveyed by revelation from the punishment of the grave, the accounting, the scale, the path, and other than that is true. And that the disbelievers are eternally [abiding] in the Fire, not the sinners among the believers, and that pardon and intercession are true by the grace of God Most High and His forgiveness. And that the signs of the Hour are true: from the emergence of the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the rising of the sun from its west, and the emergence of the beast of the earth, [all] true. And the first of the prophets is Adam, and the last of them is Muhammad, peace be upon him, and the first of the caliphs is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, may God be pleased with them all, and excellence is in this order as you have known.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is a creedal enumeration of Sunni beliefs. It begins by clarifying that evil actions are not attributed to God's pleasure, command, or love, upholding divine transcendence. Then it affirms the truth of bodily resurrection and all eschatological realities reported by revelation: the punishment of the grave, the accounting, the scale, and the path. It then states that disbelievers will abide eternally in Hell, whereas sinful believers will not, and that intercession and pardon are true by God's grace. Next, it lists the major signs of the Hour: the emergence of the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the rising of the sun from the west, and the beast of the earth—all true. Finally, it identifies Adam as the first prophet and Muhammad as the last, and it affirms the order and superiority of the four caliphs: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali, with excellence according to that sequence as is known.

Key Terms
آدم
محمد
الخلفاء
أبو بكر
عمر
عثمان
علي
الأفضلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that Ali was the first caliph or that his rank is higher than the others.
Correction: The text explicitly states the order and that excellence follows it.

Checkpoint
Who is the first caliph according to the passage?
A) Umar
B) Uthman
C) Abu Bakr
D) Ali

Key Takeaway
Adam is the first prophet, Muhammad the last; the caliphs in order of excellence are Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly honor the first caliphs in the order they deserve, or do you allow personal feelings or sectarian bias to affect your love for them? How can you actively cultivate admiration for each in their rank?
?
If Muhammad is the last prophet, what does that mean for your attitude towards anyone who claims prophethood after him? Have you ever entertained ideas that contradict this finality? What must you do to guard your faith?
?
The lesson states that excellence follows the order of the caliphs. Do you find yourself prioritizing the love of some Companions over others based on worldly reasons rather than their rank in the sight of Allah? Take a moment to sincerely examine your heart and realign your loyalties.

Unseen Matters
intermediate
5 min
The Prayer for a Decisive Argument
Commentator explains the poet's supplication for a decisive proof at questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning and scope of the poet's supplication for a sound proof at the time of questioning, including when this questioning occurs and what makes a proof valid.

Core Idea
The poet asks Allah for a proof that is correct, accepted, and valid for questioning in this life, the grave, and the Hereafter.

In this lesson, we examine the commentator's explanation of the poet's heartfelt supplication. The poet does not merely hope for any answer, but for a decisive proof—one that is sound, accepted, and religiously valid. The commentator clarifies the nuance of the request and its comprehensive scope.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the literal translation. Let the commentator's own flow guide your initial understanding.
Notice the repeated use of 'hujjatana' (our proof) and the qualifier 'mutlaqan' (absolutely).
2
Unpack key terms
Identify the key terms: الدعاء (supplication), الحجة (proof), السؤال (questioning), القيامة (Resurrection). Reflect on why these are central to this passage.
The term 'hujja' in kalam refers to a rationally compelling argument.
3
Follow the commentator's analysis
The commentator breaks down each part of the line. Note the two interpretations of 'hadha', the renewed hope in 'arju', the various recipients of the gift, and the grammatical structure.
Pay attention to the insertion of 'inda su'ali' between the two objects.
4
Grasp the scope and definition
Understand that 'mutlaqan' extends the questioning to this world, the grave, and the Hereafter. The proof must be 'sahihan maqbulan shar'iyyan' (correct, accepted, religiously valid).
This ensures the argument is both logically sound and divinely sanctioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٤٢. هَذا وَأَرْجُو اللَّهَ أَنْ يَمْنَحَنَا عِنْدَ السُّؤَالِ مُطْلَقًا حُجَّتَنَا (هَذَا) علم (۱) ، أو أسألُ الله هذا (۲) (وَأَرْجُو الله) رجاء متجددا (۳) بتَجَدُّدِ الأحوالِ والأزمنة والأمكنة (أَنْ يَمْنَحَنَا)، أي: يُعطينا معاشِرَ أهل الطاعةِ مِن المسلمين ، ويحتمل أهل العلم، ويحتمل خصوص النَّاظم، فإظهار العظمة(٤) لتأهيل الله إياه للطلب (٥) ، وذلك (٦) نعمةٌ ينبغي إظهارها ، وضمير العظمة هو المفعول الأوَّل، والثَّاني: «حُجَّتَنَا» ووسط بينهما (۷) قوله: (عِنْدَ) ورُودِ (السُّؤالِ) علينا من الغير (مُطْلَقًا ) (۸) ، أي : في الدُّنيا ، أو في القبر ، أو في القيامة (حُجَّتَنَا) ، أي ما نَحتج به احتجاجاً صحيحاً مقبولاً شرعيًّا على جوابِ ذلكَ السُّؤالِ ، بحيثُ يكون مقبولاً لا طعنَ فيه ولا امتناعَ مِن قبوله .
142. This, and I hope from Allah that He grant us, at the time of questioning absolutely, our proof. (This is) knowledge, or I ask Allah for this. (And I hope from Allah) a renewed hope with the renewal of states and times and places. (That He grant us) meaning: He give us, the group of obedient people among Muslims, and it may mean the people of knowledge, and it may mean specifically the poet. So displaying majesty is for Allah's qualifying him for the request, and that is a blessing that should be displayed. And the pronoun of majesty is the first object, and the second is 'our proof', and between them is inserted His saying: (at the) occurrence of (the questioning) upon us from others (absolutely) meaning: in this world, or in the grave, or in the Resurrection. (Our proof) meaning: what we argue with a correct, accepted, religiously valid argument in answering that question, such that it is accepted without any objection or refusal to accept it.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage is a line-by-line commentary on the poet's supplication in line 142. The commentator begins by quoting the line: 'This, and I hope from Allah that He grant us, at the time of questioning absolutely, our proof.' He then explains each part. For 'hadha' (this), he gives two possibilities: it means 'this is knowledge' or 'I ask Allah for this' (using 'hadha' as an object). 'Wa arju Allah' (and I hope from Allah) is interpreted as a renewed hope, renewed with every change of states, times, and places. 'An yamnahana' (that He grant us) is explained as giving to the obedient Muslims, or to the people of knowledge, or specifically to the poet (al-nazim). The use of the majestic plural pronoun 'na' in 'yamnahana' is to display greatness because Allah qualified the poet for the request. This is a blessing that should be shown. Grammatically, the pronoun of majesty is the first object, 'hujjatana' (our proof) is the second object, and between them is inserted the phrase 'inda su'ali' (at the time of questioning). 'Mutlaqan' (absolutely) qualifies 'su'al' and means in this world, in the grave, or in the Resurrection. Finally, 'hujjatana' is defined as that with which we argue a correct, accepted, religiously valid answer to that question, such that it is accepted without objection or refusal.

Key Terms
الدعاء
الحجة
السؤال
القيامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The supplication is only for the questioning in the grave.
Correction: The commentator explicitly states 'mutlaqan' means absolutely, covering this world, the grave, and the Resurrection.

Checkpoint
What does the poet ask Allah to grant at the time of questioning?
A) Wealth and children
B) A correct and accepted proof
C) Forgiveness of all sins
D) Long life in this world

Key Takeaway
The poet supplicates for a sound, accepted, religiously valid proof that will be effective at every questioning in this life, the grave, and the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were questioned right now about the purpose of your life, what proof (hujja) would you offer? Is it correct, accepted, and religiously valid according to the criteria in this passage, or would it crumble?
?
The poet's hope (رجاء) is renewed with every changing state. When was the last time you felt a desperate, renewed need for Allah to grant you a sound argument? What state were you in, and did you turn to Him in that moment?
?
You will face three questionings: in this life, in the grave, and on the Day of Resurrection. Which one do you honestly fear most, and what are you doing today—not tomorrow—to prepare a proof that will be accepted without objection?
